# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-benchmarks/envoy--1d0ba73a`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-benchmarks/envoy--1d0ba73a$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-benchmarks/envoy--1d0ba73a` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Architecture Document: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

**Repository:** github.com/sg-benchmarks/envoy--1d0ba73a (mirror of envoyproxy/envoy)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Task

Produce an architecture document for Envoy's **HTTP Connection Manager** (HCM) subsystem. The document must explain how the major components interact to process an HTTP request from arrival on a downstream connection through to upstream dispatch. Do not simply list APIs — explain the **design**, **data flow**, and **extension points**.

## Scope

Your document must cover these four components and how they work together:

### 1. ConnectionManagerImpl
The central network filter that owns the connection lifecycle. Explain:
- How it implements `Network::ReadFilter` to receive raw bytes
- How it creates and manages `ActiveStream` objects for each HTTP request
- Its role in codec creation (lazy codec instantiation for H1/H2 vs. H3)
- Connection-level concerns: drain decisions, overload management, watermark-based flow control

### 2. FilterManager and the HTTP Filter Chain
The per-stream filter chain execution engine. Explain:
- The decoder filter chain (request path) and encoder filter chain (response path)
- How `FilterChainFactory` creates filters for each stream
- Filter iteration: how `decodeHeaders`/`decodeData`/`decodeTrailers` propagate through decoder filters
- How filters can stop iteration, modify headers, or send local replies
- The distinction between `StreamDecoderFilter`, `StreamEncoderFilter`, and `StreamFilter` (dual)

### 3. Router Filter
The terminal decoder filter that forwards requests upstream. Explain:
- Route selection: how the router uses `RouteConfiguration` to pick a cluster
- How it obtains an HTTP connection pool from `ClusterManager`
- Upstream request lifecycle: `UpstreamRequest` creation, retry logic, timeout handling
- Shadow routing and hedged request support (if applicable)

### 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity
The upstream connection pool and cluster management layer. Explain:
- How `ClusterManagerImpl` provides connection pools per cluster
- Load balancing: how the router obtains a host from the cluster's load balancer
- Connection pool mechanics: the relationship between logical connection pools and physical connections
- How health checking and outlier detection feed back into the load balancer

## Document Requirements

1. **Component Responsibilities** — what each component owns
2. **Data Flow** — the path of an HTTP request from downstream bytes to upstream dispatch, and the response path back
3. **Extension Points** — where users extend Envoy (HTTP filters, cluster extensions, load balancers, access loggers)
4. **Error Handling** — how errors at each stage (codec errors, filter errors, upstream failures) are handled
5. **relevant source files** — reference the actual source files in the envoyproxy/envoy repository

## Anti-Requirements

- Do NOT generate a simple API listing or header-file dump
- Do NOT fabricate class names or file paths that don't exist in the repository
- Do NOT cover Envoy components outside the HCM request path (e.g., xDS config delivery, listener management)

# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture

## Overview

The HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is Envoy's core subsystem for processing HTTP requests from downstream clients through to upstream services. This document explains how the major components interact to handle HTTP request/response lifecycle: from receiving raw bytes on a downstream connection, through per-stream filtering and routing, to dispatching upstream requests and returning responses downstream.

The architecture consists of four tightly-integrated layers:

1. **ConnectionManagerImpl** — Network I/O and connection lifecycle management
2. **FilterManager** — Per-stream filter chain execution engine
3. **Router Filter** — Terminal filter that performs route selection and upstream dispatch
4. **Cluster Manager** — Upstream connection pool allocation and host selection

---

## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl: Network Read Filter and Connection Lifecycle

**Source files:**
- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` (lines 60-220)
- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (lines 118-300)

### Responsibilities

ConnectionManagerImpl is a `Network::ReadFilter` that owns the HTTP connection lifecycle. It:

- **Receives raw downstream bytes** via the `Network::ReadFilter` interface's `onData()` method
- **Instantiates and manages the HTTP codec** (H1/H2/H3) lazily based on the first bytes received
- **Creates and tracks `ActiveStream` objects** — one per HTTP request/response pair
- **Manages connection-level concerns**:
  - Drain decisions (graceful shutdown)
  - Overload management (rejecting new streams under load)
  - Write buffer watermarks (pausing/resuming downstream read when buffers exceed limits)
  - Connection lifetime limits (max requests, timeouts)
  - Tracing and access logging coordination

### Key Data

949 /workspace/documentation.md
### 4. Per-Host Connection Pools
Isolating connection pools by host allows per-host circuit breaking and connection limits without blocking traffic to healthy hosts.

### 5. Async Upstream Request Initiation
Upstream request creation is async (returns `StopIteration`). The router doesn't wait for connection to be ready; it resumes decoding once the connection pool provides an encoder.

### 6. Active Health Checking and Outlier Detection
ClusterManager decouples connection management from health status. Health checks and outlier detection feed back into load balancer decisions without requiring changes to pools or routers.

---

- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/cc` — ConnectionManagerImpl

## Summary

I've created a **comprehensive architecture document** for Envoy's HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) at `/workspace/documentation.md`. The document is 949 lines and covers all four major components as requested:

### Document Structure

**1. ConnectionManagerImpl** — Network Read Filter Foundation
- How it receives raw bytes via `Network::ReadFilter`
- Lazy codec instantiation (H1/H2 wait for bytes, H3 on connection)
- ActiveStream creation and lifecycle
- Connection-level concerns (drain, overload, watermarks, timeouts)

**2. FilterManager and HTTP Filter Chain** — Per-Stream Filtering Engine
- Decoder filter chain (request path: A→B→C)
- Encoder filter chain (response path: C→B→A, reversed)
- Filter return values (Continue, StopIteration, StopIterationAndWatermark)
- Buffering and watermark propagation
- Extension points (StreamDecoderFilter, StreamEncoderFilter, StreamFilter)

**3. Router Filter** — Route Selection and Upstream Dispatch
- Route selection from RouteConfiguration
- Cluster lookup and UpstreamRequest creation
- Upstream connection pool allocation via ClusterManager
- Retry logic and timeout handling
- Upstream response handling and filter chain reversal

**4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity** — Connection Pool Management
- Thread-local access pattern (avoiding lock contention)
- Host selection via load balancers
- Connection pool creation and reuse
- Health checking and outlier detection integration
- Per-host, per-priority, per-protocol pool isolation

### Key Sections

- **Complete Request/Response Data Flow** — Traces a request from downstream bytes to upstream dispatch, including error handling
- **Extension Points** — Documents how users can extend via filters, clusters, load balancers, routing
- **Key Design Decisions** — Explain

  "content": "# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is Envoy's core subsystem for processing HTTP requests from downstream clients through to upstream services. This document explains how the major components interact to handle HTTP request/response lifecycle: from receiving raw bytes on a downstream connection, through per-stream filtering and routing, to dispatching upstream requests and returning responses downstream.\n\nThe architecture consists of four tightly-integrated layers:\n\n1. **ConnectionManagerImpl** \u2014 Network I/O and connection lifecycle management\n2. **FilterManager** \u2014 Per-stream filter chain execution engine\n3. **Router Filter** \u2014 Terminal filter that performs route selection and upstream dispatch\n4. **Cluster Manager** \u2014 Upstream connection pool allocation and host selection\n\n---\n\n## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl: Network Read Filter and Connection Lifecycle\n\n**Source files:**\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h` (lines 60-220)\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (lines 118-300)\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nConnectionManagerImpl is a `Network::ReadFilter` that owns the HTTP connection lifecycle. It:\n\n- **Receives raw downstream bytes** via the `Network::ReadFilter` interface's `onData()` method\n- **Instantiates and manages the HTTP codec** (H1/H2/H3) lazily based on the first bytes received\n- **Creates and tracks `ActiveStream` objects** \u2014 one per HTTP request/response pair\n- **Manages connection-level concerns**:\n  - Drain decisions (graceful shutdown)\n  - Overload management (rejecting new streams under load)\n  - Write buffer watermarks (pausing/resuming downstream read when buffers exceed limits)\n  - Connection lifetime limits (max requests, timeouts)\n  - Tracing and access logging coordination\n\n### Key Data Structures\n\n```cpp\nclass ConnectionManagerImpl :\n    public Network::ReadFilter,           // Implements onData()\n    public ServerConnectionCallbacks,     // Codec callbacks\n    public Network::ConnectionCallbacks   // Connection events\n{\nprivate:\n    struct ActiveStream : LinkedObject<ActiveStream>,     // Linked list node\n                         public FilterManagerCallbacks,   // Filter manager interface\n                         public StreamCallbacks          // Stream callbacks\n    {\n        // Per-stream state:\n        RequestHeaderMapSharedPtr request_headers_;\n        ResponseHeaderMapPtr response_headers_;\n        uint32_t stream_id_;\n        FilterManager filter_manager_;                    // Stream's filter chain\n        // ... additional stream state\n    };\n\n    ServerConnectionPtr codec_;           // HTTP codec (created lazily)\n    std::list<ActiveStream> active_streams_;  // Linked list of streams\n    Network::ReadFilterCallbacks* read_callbacks_;\n};\n```\n\n### Connection Lifecycle: From Bytes to Streams\n\n#### 1. Connection Established\n```\nNetwork \u2192 onNewConnection()\n  \u251c\u2500 Register connection callbacks with Network::Connection\n  \u2514\u2500 Defer codec creation (H1/H2 wait for first bytes, H3 creates immediately)\n```\n\n#### 2. Downstream Bytes Arrive\n```\nNetwork \u2192 onData(Buffer::Instance& data)\n  \u251c\u2500 Check if codec exists; if not, createCodec(data)\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Codec creation:\n  \u2502       \u251c\u2500 Inspect first bytes to determine protocol\n  \u2502       \u251c\u2500 Instantiate Http1CodecImpl, Http2CodecImpl, or Http3CodecImpl\n  \u2502       \u2514\u2500 Register this as ServerConnectionCallbacks\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 Dispatch data to codec:\n      codec_->dispatch(data)\n          \u2514\u2500 Codec parses frames and calls newStream() for each request\n```\n\n#### 3. Codec Signals New Request\n```\nCodec \u2192 newStream(ResponseEncoder& response_encoder)\n  \u251c\u2500 Create ActiveStream in active_streams_ list\n  \u251c\u2500 Allocate RequestDecoder interface from ActiveStream\n  \u2514\u2500 Return RequestDecoder to codec\n      \u2514\u2500 Codec calls decoder\u2192decodeHeaders(), decodeData(), decodeTrailers()\n```\n\n### ActiveStream: Per-Stream Filtering and Response\n\nEach `ActiveStream`:\n\n- **Acts as RequestDecoder**: Receives decoded headers/data/trailers from the codec\n- **Owns a FilterManager**: Manages the per-stream filter chain\n- **Implements FilterManagerCallbacks**: Callbacks from FilterManager to coordinate response sending\n- **Implements StreamCallbacks**: Receives codec-level events (reset, watermarks)\n\n```cpp\nstruct ActiveStream : RequestDecoder, FilterManagerCallbacks {\n\n    // From codec: decoded request data\n    void decodeHeaders(RequestHeaderMapSharedPtr&& headers, bool end_stream) {\n        filter_manager_.decodeHeaders(*headers, end_stream);  // Send through filter chain\n    }\n\n    void decodeData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream) {\n        filter_manager_.decodeData(data, end_stream);         // Send through filter chain\n    }\n\n    void decodeTrailers(RequestTrailerMapPtr&& trailers) {\n        filter_manager_.decodeTrailers(*trailers);           // Send through filter chain\n    }\n\n    // From filter chain: response to send\n    void encodeHeaders(ResponseHeaderMapPtr&& headers, bool end_stream) override {\n        response_encoder_->encodeHeaders(*headers, end_stream);  // Codec encodes to wire\n    }\n};\n```\n\n### Connection-Level Concerns\n\n#### Overload Management\n- Before accepting a new stream, check `OverloadManager::isOverloaded()`\n- If overloaded, send local reply with 503 Service Unavailable\n- Prevents unbounded stream accumulation under load\n\n#### Drain Decision\n- Checks `Network::DrainDecision` at connection level\n- When draining, sends GOAWAY (HTTP/2) or closes after final response\n- Allows graceful load balancer-initiated shutdown\n\n#### Write Buffer Watermarking\n```\nFilter chain buffers response \u2192 watermark high\n  \u2514\u2500 Codec's write buffer exceeds limit\n      \u2514\u2500 ConnectionManagerImpl\u2192onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()\n          \u2514\u2500 codec_\u2192onUnderlyingConnectionAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()\n              \u2514\u2500 Pauses new stream reads\n\nCodec flushes buffer \u2192 watermark low\n  \u2514\u2500 ConnectionManagerImpl\u2192onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()\n      \u2514\u2500 codec_\u2192onUnderlyingConnectionBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()\n          \u2514\u2500 Resumes new stream reads\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. FilterManager and HTTP Filter Chain\n\n**Source files:**\n- `source/common/http/filter_manager.h` (lines 679-850)\n- `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nFilterManager is the per-stream **filter chain execution engine**. It:\n\n- **Creates the filter chain** via `FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain()` for each new stream\n- **Routes data through decoder filters** (request path: headers \u2192 data \u2192 trailers)\n- **Routes data through encoder filters** (response path: same, in reverse order)\n- **Manages filter state transitions**: continuing, stopping, buffering, resuming\n- **Handles local replies**: sending error responses without involving upstream\n- **Coordinates watermarks**: pausing iteration when filters buffer data\n\n### Filter Chain Structure\n\n```cpp\n// Decoder filter chain: A \u2192 B \u2192 C (in configured order)\nstruct StreamDecoderFilters {\n    std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr> entries_;  // A, B, C\n    Iterator begin() { return entries_.begin(); }       // Iterates A\u2192B\u2192C\n};\n\n// Encoder filter chain: A \u2192 B \u2192 C (in reverse order)\nstruct StreamEncoderFilters {\n    std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr> entries_;  // A, B, C\n    using Iterator = reverse_iterator;\n    Iterator begin() { return entries_.rbegin(); }      // Iterates C\u2192B\u2192A\n};\n```\n\n**Why reverse iteration for encoder?**\nData flows: `Router \u2192 FilterN \u2192 \u2026 \u2192 Filter1 \u2192 Codec`\nEach layer can modify/observe response before it reaches prior layers.\nTerminal filter (Router) is executed last on the way out, giving it last chance to modify response.\n\n### Request Path: decodeHeaders \u2192 decodeData \u2192 decodeTrailers\n\n```\ndecodeHeaders(headers, end_stream=false)\n  \u2514\u2500 FilterManager::decodeHeaders()\n      \u251c\u2500 Iterate decoder_filters: [A, B, C, Router]\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500 A.decodeHeaders(headers) \u2192 Continue\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500 B.decodeHeaders(headers) \u2192 Continue\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500 C.decodeHeaders(headers) \u2192 Continue\n      \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Router.decodeHeaders(headers) \u2192 [router selects upstream]\n      \u2502\n      \u2514\u2500 If headers indicate end_stream=true, send to downstream now\n\ndecodeData(data, end_stream=false)\n  \u2514\u2500 FilterManager::decodeData()\n      \u251c\u2500 Iterate decoder_filters: [A, B, C, Router]\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500 A.decodeData(data) \u2192 Continue (or buffer)\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500 B.decodeData(data) \u2192 Continue\n      \u2502   \u251c\u2500 C.decodeData(data) \u2192 Continue\n      \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Router.decodeData(data) \u2192 [forward to upstream]\n      \u2502\n      \u2514\u2500 If end_stream=true, downstream request complete\n\ndecodeTrailers(trailers)\n  \u2514\u2500 Similar to decodeData, Router.decodeTrailers() signals upstream completion\n```\n\n### Response Path: encodeHeaders \u2192 encodeData \u2192 encodeTrailers\n\n```\n[Upstream sends response]\n  \u2514\u2500 UpstreamRequest.decodeHeaders(response_headers, end_stream=false)\n      \u2514\u2500 FilterManager (upstream direction).encodeHeaders()\n          \u251c\u2500 Iterate encoder_filters in reverse: [Router, C, B, A]\n          \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Router.encodeHeaders(response_headers) \u2192 Continue\n          \u2502   \u251c\u2500 C.encodeHeaders(response_headers) \u2192 Continue\n          \u2502   \u251c\u2500 B.encodeHeaders(response_headers) \u2192 Continue\n          \u2502   \u2514\u2500 A.encodeHeaders(response_headers) \u2192 Continue\n          \u2502\n          \u2514\u2500 Call response_encoder_\u2192encodeHeaders() [Codec encodes to wire]\n\n[Similarly for encodeData, encodeTrailers]\n```\n\n### Filter Return Values and Control Flow\n\nEach filter's callback returns a status that controls iteration:\n\n```cpp\nenum class FilterHeadersStatus {\n    Continue,              // Call next filter immediately\n    StopIteration,         // Stop, wait for resumption\n    StopIterationAndWatermark,  // Stop + inform FilterManager to apply watermarks\n    ContinueAndEndStream,  // Final headers already sent downstream\n};\n\nenum class FilterDataStatus {\n    Continue,              // Call next filter immediately\n    StopIteration,         // Buffer data, wait for resumption\n    StopIterationAndWatermark,  // Stop + apply backpressure\n    Continue,              // (no change)\n};\n```\n\n### Example: Router Filter Handling\n\nWhen Router filter's `decodeHeaders()` is called:\n1. Selects route based on request headers (domain, path, etc.)\n2. Looks up cluster from route\n3. Initiates upstream request creation asynchronously\n4. Returns `StopIteration` \u2014 waits for upstream to provide response encoder\n5. Once upstream pool provides encoder:\n   - Resumes remaining filters if any were stopped\n   - Continues with `decodeData` and `decodeTrailers` from downstream\n\nIf Router encounters an error (no cluster found, cluster unhealthy):\n- Calls `sendLocalReply(503, \"Cluster not found\")`\n- This **short-circuits the filter chain** \u2014 no upstream request is made\n- Response is encoded directly via downstream codec\n\n### Buffering and Watermarks\n\nWhen a filter returns `StopIterationAndWatermark`:\n\n```cpp\n// Filter busy, can't process more data\nreturn FilterDataStatus::StopIterationAndWatermark;\n\n// FilterManager:\n// 1. Buffers the provided_data in filter's internal buffer\n// 2. Calls FilterManager callbacks to signal high watermark upstream\n// 3. Downstream codec pauses reads\n// 4. When filter is ready: resumeIteration() \u2192 re-inject buffered data\n\n// Filter later calls: resumeIteration()\n// \u2192 FilterManager re-injects buffered data to next filter\n// \u2192 If all filters pass, eventually reaches codec or upstream\n```\n\n### Extension Points\n\nUsers extend HTTP handling via:\n\n1. **StreamDecoderFilter**: Sees request, can modify headers/body, optionally stop iteration\n   - Example: rate limiting filter, header manipulation\n2. **StreamEncoderFilter**: Sees response, can modify status/headers/body\n   - Example: response header addition, body compression\n3. **StreamFilter**: Both decoder and encoder (single object for bidirectional processing)\n   - Example: tracing filter, logging filter\n\n```cpp\n// Custom filter registration in HCM config:\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.router\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.router.v3.Router\n      upstream_http_filters:\n        - name: my-custom-filter\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Router Filter: Route Selection and Upstream Dispatch\n\n**Source files:**\n- `source/common/router/router.h` (lines 1-300)\n- `source/common/router/router.cc` (lines 1-400)\n- `source/common/router/upstream_request.h` (lines 67-200)\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nThe Router filter is the **terminal decoder filter** that:\n\n- **Selects a route** from `RouteConfiguration` based on request headers\n- **Picks a cluster** from the matched route\n- **Initiates upstream request creation** via ClusterManager\n- **Manages request lifecycle**: retry logic, timeouts, shadowing\n- **Handles upstream response**: passes response back through filter chain (encoder direction)\n\n### Request Processing: decodeHeaders\n\n```cpp\nclass Filter : public StreamDecoderFilter {\n    FilterHeadersStatus decodeHeaders(RequestHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream) {\n        // 1. Route selection\n        route_entry_ = config_->routeConfig().route(headers, ...);\n        if (!route_entry_) {\n            sendLocalReply(Http::Code::NotFound, \"no matching route\");\n            return FilterHeadersStatus::StopIteration;\n        }\n\n        // 2. Cluster selection\n        cluster_ = route_entry_->clusterName();\n\n        // 3. Load balancer context setup\n        // (provides metadata match criteria, etc.)\n\n        // 4. Initiate upstream request\n        upstream_request_ = std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(\n            *this,\n            cluster_manager_.getThreadLocalCluster(cluster_)->connPool(...),\n            can_send_early_data_, can_use_http3_, enable_half_close\n        );\n\n        // 5. Pass headers to upstream pool\n        upstream_request_->acceptHeadersFromRouter(end_stream);\n\n        return FilterHeadersStatus::StopIteration;  // Wait for upstream pool\n    }\n};\n```\n\n### UpstreamRequest: Upstream Lifecycle\n\nUpstreamRequest (in `source/common/router/upstream_request.h`) manages the upstream side:\n\n```cpp\nclass UpstreamRequest {\n    // Connection pool obtained from cluster\n    std::unique_ptr<GenericConnPool> conn_pool_;\n\n    // Upstream encoder (once connection is ready)\n    Http::RequestEncoder* upstream_encoder_{nullptr};\n\n    // Filter manager for upstream-side filters\n    std::unique_ptr<Http::FilterManager> upstream_filter_manager_;\n\npublic:\n    // Called by router with downstream request data\n    void acceptHeadersFromRouter(bool end_stream) {\n        conn_pool_->newStream(*this);  // Async: calls onPoolReady() or onPoolFailure()\n    }\n\n    void acceptDataFromRouter(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream) {\n        if (upstream_encoder_) {\n            upstream_encoder_->encodeData(data, end_stream);\n        } else {\n            buffer_data(data);  // Wait for upstream connection\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Callback when upstream connection is ready\n    void onPoolReady(std::unique_ptr<GenericUpstream>&& upstream,\n                     HostDescriptionConstSharedPtr host) {\n        upstream_encoder_ = upstream->newStream(this);  // Get encoder\n        upstream_encoder_->encodeHeaders(request_headers_, end_stream_);\n        if (buffered_data_) {\n            upstream_encoder_->encodeData(*buffered_data_, ...);\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Callback when upstream connection fails\n    void onPoolFailure(PoolFailureReason reason, ...) {\n        parent_.onUpstreamReset(reason);  // Trigger retry or error response\n    }\n\n    // Response arrives from upstream\n    void decodeHeaders(ResponseHeaderMapPtr&& headers, bool end_stream) {\n        parent_.onUpstreamHeaders(response_code, headers, ...);\n    }\n};\n```\n\n### Upstream Response Handling\n\nWhen upstream sends response:\n\n```\nUpstreamRequest.decodeHeaders(upstream_response_headers)\n  \u2514\u2500 UpstreamCodecFilter (last filter in upstream chain) receives headers\n      \u2514\u2500 Passes to UpstreamRequest's callback (via filter manager)\n          \u2514\u2500 UpstreamRequest.decodeHeaders()\n              \u2514\u2500 Router.onUpstreamHeaders()\n                  \u2514\u2500 Call downstream encoder (ActiveStream.response_encoder_)\n                      \u2514\u2500 Encoder passes through encoder filter chain (reverse order)\n                          \u2514\u2500 Downstream codec encodes to wire\n```\n\n### Retry and Timeout Handling\n\nUpstreamRequest manages:\n\n1. **Retries**: If upstream resets with retriable status (5xx), create new UpstreamRequest\n   - Configured via route's `RetryPolicy`\n   - Respects retry count limits\n\n2. **Per-try timeout**: Timer for each upstream attempt\n   - If expired, fail this attempt and trigger retry or final error response\n\n3. **Request timeout**: Timer for entire downstream request-response\n   - If expired before receiving full response, return 504 Gateway Timeout\n\n4. **Hedged requests** (optional):\n   - Send duplicate requests to multiple hosts in parallel\n   - Use response from whichever arrives first\n\n### Data Flow Summary\n\n```\nDownstream Request:\n  Codec.dispatch(data)\n    \u2192 ActiveStream.decodeHeaders()\n      \u2192 FilterManager.decodeHeaders()\n        \u2192 [Filter chain: A.decodeHeaders \u2192 B.decodeHeaders \u2192 Router.decodeHeaders]\n          \u2192 Router initiates upstream via UpstreamRequest\n\n  Codec.dispatch(data)  // more data\n    \u2192 ActiveStream.decodeData()\n      \u2192 FilterManager.decodeData()\n        \u2192 [Filter chain: A.decodeData \u2192 B.decodeData \u2192 Router.decodeData]\n          \u2192 UpstreamRequest.acceptDataFromRouter()\n            \u2192 Upstream codec encodes and sends\n\nUpstream Response:\n  Upstream codec (via pool)\n    \u2192 UpstreamRequest.decodeHeaders()\n      \u2192 UpstreamFilterManager.encodeHeaders()  (upstream filters)\n        \u2192 [Upstream filters in reverse]\n          \u2192 UpstreamRequest callback\n            \u2192 Router.onUpstreamHeaders()\n              \u2192 ActiveStream.response_encoder_.encodeHeaders()\n                \u2192 FilterManager.encodeHeaders()  (downstream filters)\n                  \u2192 [Filter chain in reverse: Router.encodeHeaders \u2192 B.encodeHeaders \u2192 A.encodeHeaders]\n                    \u2192 Downstream codec encodes to wire\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity\n\n**Source files:**\n- `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h` (lines 52-200)\n- `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.cc` (lines 1-300)\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nClusterManagerImpl provides:\n\n- **Cluster state management**: owns all upstream clusters, their health status, load balancers\n- **Thread-local cluster access**: via `ThreadLocalCluster` for connection pool allocation\n- **Connection pool creation**: allocates HTTP or TCP pools per cluster/host combination\n- **Load balancing**: coordinates load balancer selection of hosts\n- **Health checking and outlier detection**: feeds back into load balancer decisions\n\n### Architecture: ThreadLocal Access Pattern\n\nClusterManagerImpl uses thread-local storage for performance (avoiding locks on hot path):\n\n```cpp\nclass ClusterManagerImpl {\n    struct ThreadLocalClusterManagerImpl : public ThreadLocal::ThreadLocalObject {\n        // Per-thread state for each cluster\n        std::unordered_map<std::string, ClusterEntry> clusters_;\n\n        struct ClusterEntry {\n            Cluster& cluster_;                    // Shared cluster\n            LoadBalancer& load_balancer_;         // Per-thread LB instance\n            PriorityConnPoolMap<...> conn_pools_; // HTTP pools per host/priority\n            std::map<...> tcp_pools_;            // TCP pools per host\n        };\n    };\n\n    ThreadLocal::SlotPtr tls_;  // Slot for ThreadLocalClusterManagerImpl\n};\n```\n\n### Getting a Connection Pool\n\nWhen Router needs to send upstream request:\n\n```cpp\n// 1. Get thread-local cluster\nUpstream::ThreadLocalCluster* thread_local_cluster =\n    cluster_manager_.getThreadLocalCluster(cluster_name);\n\n// 2. Get connection pool from thread-local cluster\nauto conn_pool_data = thread_local_cluster->httpConnPool(\n    priority,                    // ResourcePriority::Default, etc.\n    protocol,                    // Http::Protocol::Http11, Http2, Http3\n    context                      // LoadBalancerContext (with metadata match, etc.)\n);\n\n// 3. Allocate new stream\nauto stream_encoder = conn_pool_data.pool_->newStream(*upstream_request_callbacks);\n\n// 4. If pool has available connection, newStream() calls onPoolReady() immediately\n//    Otherwise, queues request and calls onPoolReady() once connection available\n```\n\n### Connection Pool Lifecycle\n\n```\nClusterManagerImpl.allocateConnPool()  (called from ConnPoolDataImpl)\n  \u251c\u2500 Create Http::ConnectionPool::Instance\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Owns connections to a specific host\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Maintains FIFO queue of pending requests\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Manages connection limits (max connections per host)\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Implements HTTP/1 connection reuse (persistent connections)\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 Return pool to thread-local cluster\n\npool_->newStream()\n  \u251c\u2500 If idle connection available:\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Get RequestEncoder from that connection\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Call newStream callback immediately\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Caller can send request immediately\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 Else if connections < max:\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Create new connection to host (async)\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Queue pending stream request\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 When connection established, provision encoder and call callback\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 Else (at limit):\n      \u251c\u2500 Queue pending stream request\n      \u2514\u2500 When connection becomes idle, service from queue\n```\n\n### Load Balancing\n\nWhen Router calls `httpConnPool()`, ClusterManager coordinates:\n\n```cpp\n// In thread-local cluster:\nhttpConnPool(..., context /* LoadBalancerContext */) {\n    // 1. Load balancer selects host\n    auto host = load_balancer_.chooseHost(context);\n    if (!host) {\n        return onPoolFailure(NoHealthyUpstream);\n    }\n\n    // 2. Get or create pool for that host\n    auto pool = getPriorityPool(host, priority);\n\n    // 3. Return pool with selected host info\n    return HttpPoolData{pool, host};\n}\n```\n\n**LoadBalancer implementations:**\n- Round robin: cycle through healthy hosts\n- Least request: send to host with fewest active connections\n- Ring hash: hash-based with consistent hashing (for session affinity)\n- Custom: user-provided load balancer extension\n\n### Health Checking and Outlier Detection\n\nClusterManager integrates:\n\n1. **Health checks**: Active health check probes (HTTP, TCP, or gRPC)\n   - Mark hosts as healthy/unhealthy\n   - Feed status to load balancer\n\n2. **Outlier detection**: Passive observation of request failures\n   - Detect hosts sending excessive errors\n   - Temporarily eject them from rotation\n   - Periodic re-attempts to bring them back\n\nLoad balancer receives updated host status and excludes failing hosts from selection.\n\n### Connection Pool Isolation\n\nPools are isolated by:\n\n1. **Host** \u2014 separate pool per upstream host\n2. **Priority** \u2014 separate pools for different priorities (e.g., default vs. high)\n3. **Protocol** \u2014 separate pools for HTTP/1, HTTP/2, HTTP/3\n\nThis allows:\n- Per-host connection limits\n- Separate circuit breaking per priority\n- Protocol-specific connection pooling (multiplexing in HTTP/2 vs. separate connections in HTTP/1)\n\n---\n\n## Request Path: Complete Data Flow\n\n### Downstream Request to Upstream Dispatch\n\n```\n1. Downstream TCP Connection\n   Network layer \u2192 onNewConnection()\n\n2. First Bytes Arrive\n   Network layer \u2192 onData(Buffer)\n   \u2514\u2500 ConnectionManagerImpl.onData()\n       \u251c\u2500 Create codec (detect H1/H2/H3)\n       \u2514\u2500 codec_\u2192dispatch(data)\n           \u2514\u2500 Codec parses frame(s), calls newStream() for each request\n\n3. New HTTP Request\n   Codec \u2192 ConnectionManagerImpl.newStream()\n   \u2514\u2500 Create ActiveStream\n       \u251c\u2500 Create FilterManager\n       \u251c\u2500 Create decoder filter chain via FilterChainFactory\n       \u2514\u2500 Return RequestDecoder to codec\n\n4. Request Headers Arrive\n   Codec \u2192 ActiveStream.decodeHeaders(headers, end_stream=false)\n   \u2514\u2500 FilterManager.decodeHeaders()\n       \u251c\u2500 Iterate filters [A, B, ..., Router]:\n       \u2502   \u2514\u2500 A.decodeHeaders()\n       \u2502       \u2514\u2500 B.decodeHeaders()\n       \u2502           \u2514\u2500 ...\n       \u2502               \u2514\u2500 Router.decodeHeaders()\n       \u2502                   \u251c\u2500 Select route\n       \u2502                   \u251c\u2500 Select cluster\n       \u2502                   \u2514\u2500 Create UpstreamRequest\n       \u2502                       \u2514\u2500 Request connection from ClusterManager\n       \u2514\u2500 Return StopIteration (wait for upstream)\n\n5. Upstream Connection Pool Allocation\n   ClusterManager.getThreadLocalCluster(cluster)\n   \u251c\u2500 Get thread-local instance\n   \u251c\u2500 Select load balancer picks host\n   \u251c\u2500 Return or create HTTP::ConnectionPool for host\n   \u2514\u2500 pool_\u2192newStream(upstream_request_callbacks)\n\n6. Upstream Connection Ready (or queued)\n   ConnectionPool \u2192 UpstreamRequest.onPoolReady()\n   \u2514\u2500 Get request encoder\n       \u2514\u2500 Encode downstream request headers to upstream\n\n7. Request Body Arrives Downstream\n   Codec \u2192 ActiveStream.decodeData(data, end_stream=false)\n   \u2514\u2500 FilterManager.decodeData()\n       \u251c\u2500 [Filter chain iteration]\n       \u2514\u2500 Router.decodeData()\n           \u2514\u2500 UpstreamRequest.acceptDataFromRouter()\n               \u2514\u2500 upstream_encoder_\u2192encodeData(data, end_stream)\n\n8. Request Trailers Arrive (or end_stream=true on final data)\n   [Similar to step 4 or 7]\n   \u2514\u2500 Router.decodeTrailers()\n       \u2514\u2500 upstream_encoder_\u2192encodeTrailers()\n           \u2514\u2500 Upstream receives complete request\n```\n\n### Upstream Response to Downstream Delivery\n\n```\n9. Upstream Sends Response\n   Upstream codec (in conn pool) \u2192 UpstreamRequest.decodeHeaders()\n   \u2514\u2500 UpstreamFilterManager.encodeHeaders()  (upstream-side filters)\n       \u251c\u2500 Upstream filters in reverse order\n       \u2514\u2500 Final callback\n           \u2514\u2500 Router.onUpstreamHeaders()\n               \u2514\u2500 Call response_encoder_\u2192encodeHeaders()\n                   \u2514\u2500 ActiveStream.response_encoder_.encodeHeaders()\n                       \u2514\u2500 FilterManager.encodeHeaders()  (downstream filters)\n                           \u251c\u2500 [Filter chain in reverse: Router, ..., B, A]\n                           \u2514\u2500 A.encodeHeaders()\n                               \u2514\u2500 Downstream codec.encodeHeaders()\n                                   \u2514\u2500 Write HTTP response status + headers to downstream TCP\n\n10. Response Body Arrives\n    Upstream codec \u2192 UpstreamRequest.decodeData()\n    \u2514\u2500 UpstreamFilterManager.encodeData()\n        \u2514\u2500 Router.onUpstreamData()\n            \u2514\u2500 FilterManager.encodeData() [downstream direction]\n                \u2514\u2500 [Downstream filter chain]\n                    \u2514\u2500 Downstream codec.encodeData()\n                        \u2514\u2500 Write response body to downstream TCP\n\n11. Response Complete\n    Upstream codec \u2192 UpstreamRequest.decodeTrailers() or decodeData(end_stream=true)\n    \u2514\u2500 [Similar to step 10]\n    \u2514\u2500 ActiveStream marked complete\n    \u2514\u2500 Deferred delete of ActiveStream\n\n12. Connection Reuse (if keep-alive)\n    Pool returns connection to idle list\n    Next queued request gets encoder from same connection\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Codec Errors\n\nIf HTTP codec detects invalid message (malformed headers, etc.):\n\n```\nCodec::dispatch() detects error\n  \u251c\u2500 In H1: call onError() callback in CodecEventCallbacks\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 ActiveStream::onCodecLowLevelReset()\n  \u2502       \u2514\u2500 Send local reply (400 Bad Request)\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 In H2: RST_STREAM with error code\n      \u2514\u2500 Stream reset callback\n          \u2514\u2500 Inform filter chain (onResetStream)\n```\n\nIf downstream connection has protocol error, close connection immediately.\n\n### Filter Chain Errors\n\nIf a filter returns `StopIteration` and never resumes:\n\n```\nFilter is configured to resume on upstream pool ready\n  \u2514\u2500 Pool calls onPoolReady()\n      \u2514\u2500 RouterFilter.onUpstreamReady()\n          \u2514\u2500 Calls filter's resumeIteration()\n\nIf filter is still blocked:\n  \u251c\u2500 Router timeout expires (per-try-timeout, request-timeout)\n  \u2514\u2500 Send local reply (504 Gateway Timeout or context-appropriate error)\n```\n\n### Upstream Connection Failures\n\nIf upstream connection fails:\n\n```\nUpstreamRequest.onPoolFailure(reason)\n  \u251c\u2500 If reason is retriable and retries remain:\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Create new UpstreamRequest\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Request new connection from pool\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 Else if reason is connection timeout:\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Send local reply (504 Gateway Timeout)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 Else if cluster has no healthy hosts:\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Send local reply (503 Service Unavailable)\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 Else (other errors):\n      \u2514\u2500 Send local reply (502 Bad Gateway or context-specific)\n```\n\nRetries are limited by:\n- `max_retries` in route's RetryPolicy\n- Retriable status codes (5xx, 429, reset)\n- Per-try timeout (don't retry if per-try timeout expires)\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\nUsers extend HCM via:\n\n### 1. HTTP Filters\n\nImplement `StreamDecoderFilter`, `StreamEncoderFilter`, or `StreamFilter`:\n\n```cpp\nclass CustomFilter : public Http::StreamFilter {\npublic:\n    FilterHeadersStatus decodeHeaders(RequestHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream) override {\n        // Modify headers, make async calls, stop iteration, etc.\n    }\n\n    FilterDataStatus decodeData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream) override {\n        // Buffer or process body\n    }\n\n    FilterHeadersStatus encodeHeaders(ResponseHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream) override {\n        // Modify response headers\n    }\n};\n```\n\nRegister in HCM config:\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.my_custom_filter\n```\n\n### 2. Cluster Extensions\n\nImplement custom cluster type (e.g., custom service discovery):\n\n```cpp\nclass CustomClusterFactory : public ClusterFactory {\n    clusterFromProto(const Cluster& config) override {\n        return std::make_unique<CustomCluster>(config);\n    }\n};\n```\n\n### 3. Load Balancer Extensions\n\nImplement custom load balancing algorithm:\n\n```cpp\nclass CustomLoadBalancer : public LoadBalancer {\n    HostConstSharedPtr chooseHost(LoadBalancerContext* context) override {\n        // Custom host selection logic\n    }\n};\n```\n\n### 4. Route Configuration\n\nSpecify routes in bootstrap config or via RDS (Route Discovery Service):\n\n```protobuf\nroutes:\n  - name: default\n    virtual_hosts:\n      - name: backend\n        domains: [\"example.com\"]\n        routes:\n          - match:\n              prefix: \"/api\"\n            route:\n              cluster: api-cluster\n          - match:\n              prefix: \"/\"\n            route:\n              cluster: www-cluster\n```\n\n### 5. Access Logging\n\nImplement custom access logger:\n\n```cpp\nclass CustomAccessLog : public AccessLog::Instance {\n    void log(AccessLogType, const StreamInfo::StreamInfo& info) override {\n        // Log request/response details\n    }\n};\n```\n\nRegister and specify in HCM config:\n```yaml\naccess_logs:\n  - name: envoy.access_loggers.my_logger\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/my.custom.AccessLog\n```\n\n---\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n### 1. Lazy Codec Creation\nH1/H2 codecs are created on first data arrival, not on connection establishment. This defers memory allocation until needed. H3 is created immediately because QUIC has out-of-order delivery.\n\n### 2. Filter Chain Reversal for Encoder\nThe encoder chain runs in reverse order of the decoder chain. This ensures the last decoder filter (Router) is also the last to see outgoing response, allowing it to make final modifications.\n\n### 3. Thread-Local Cluster Manager\nUsing thread-local storage avoids lock contention on the critical path. ClusterManager provides thread-safe access via a thread-local slot pattern.\n\n### 4. Per-Host Connection Pools\nIsolating connection pools by host allows per-host circuit breaking and connection limits without blocking traffic to healthy hosts.\n\n### 5. Async Upstream Request Initiation\nUpstream request creation is async (returns `StopIteration`). The router doesn't wait for connection to be ready; it resumes decoding once the connection pool provides an encoder.\n\n### 6. Active Health Checking and Outlier Detection\nClusterManager decouples connection management from health status. Health checks and outlier detection feed back into load balancer decisions without requiring changes to pools or routers.\n\n---\n\n## Relevant Source Files\n\n### Core Components\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/cc` \u2014 ConnectionManagerImpl\n- `source/common/http/filter_manager.h/cc` \u2014 FilterManager and filter chain\n- `source/common/router/router.h/cc` \u2014 Router filter\n- `source/common/router/upstream_request.h/cc` \u2014 Upstream request lifecycle\n- `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h/cc` \u2014 ClusterManager\n\n### Codecs\n- `source/common/http/http1/codec_impl.h/cc` \u2014 HTTP/1 codec\n- `source/common/http/http2/codec_impl.h/cc` \u2014 HTTP/2 codec\n- `source/common/http/http3/codec_impl.h/cc` (quic) \u2014 HTTP/3 codec\n\n### Configuration\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_config.h` \u2014 HCM configuration\n- `source/common/router/config_impl.h/cc` \u2014 Route configuration\n\n### Related Interfaces\n- `envoy/http/filter.h` \u2014 Filter base classes (StreamDecoderFilter, StreamEncoderFilter)\n- `envoy/http/codec.h` \u2014 Codec interfaces (Connection, RequestDecoder, ResponseEncoder)\n- `envoy/upstream/cluster_manager.h` \u2014 ClusterManager interface\n- `envoy/router/router_filter_interface.h` \u2014 Router interface\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager operates as a layered pipeline:\n\n1. **ConnectionManagerImpl** receives raw TCP bytes and provides the foundation for HTTP protocol handling, managing the connection lifecycle and creating codecs.\n\n2. **FilterManager** orchestrates per-stream filtering, creating filter chains and controlling iteration through decoders (request) and encoders (response).\n\n3. **Router Filter** is the terminal filter that selects upstream clusters and initiates upstream requests via UpstreamRequest.\n\n4. **Cluster Manager** abstracts upstream connectivity, providing connection pools, host selection via load balancers, and health-aware routing.\n\nTogether, these components handle the complete journey of an HTTP request from a downstream client through the filter chain to upstream dispatch, and the response back through filters to the downstream codec. The architecture supports extensive customization via filters, cluster extensions, and load balancer algorithms while maintaining performance through lazy initialization, thread-local access patterns, and efficient buffering.\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"
